  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0da70a07-c213-4e26-9a9a-7f3231524572'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11965945163659195327">Twenty-five-year-old Venetia Lanyon's beauty is rivaled only by her sensibility. Intelligent and independent, her future seems safe and predictable. Lovely Venetia despairs of ever meeting the handsome hero of her romantic dreams but is nearly resigned to spinsterhood, thanks to the enormous amount of responsibility she inherited with a Yorkshire estate and an invalid but </span>
  <span id="freeText11965945163659195327" style="display:none">Twenty-five-year-old Venetia Lanyon's beauty is rivaled only by her sensibility. Intelligent and independent, her future seems safe and predictable. Lovely Venetia despairs of ever meeting the handsome hero of her romantic dreams but is nearly resigned to spinsterhood, thanks to the enormous amount of responsibility she inherited with a Yorkshire estate and an invalid but precocious brother, Aubrey. She lives in comfortable seclusion in rural Yorkshire, she has never been further than Harrogate, nor enjoyed the lackluster attentions of any but her two wearisomely persistent suitors. She can not accept to marry the respectable but dull Edward Yardley - she will only marry for love.<br /><br />Then her long-absent neighbor, thirty-eight-year-old Lord Jasper Damerel, returns home to Yorkshire. In one extraordinary encounter, she meets the infamous neighbor, who she knows only by reputation - a gamester, a shocking rake, and a man of sadly unsteady character - and before she knows better, she finds friendship with a libertine whose way of life has scandalised the North Riding for years. Lord Damerel finds Venetia to be the most truly engaging and wittily perverse female he has encountered in all his life and determined to woo and win her, he pursues her with a passionate abandon that is soon the talk of the ton. And after her encounter with the dashing, dangerous rake, Venetia's well-ordered life is turned upside down, and she embarks upon a courtship with him that scandalises and horrifies the whole community.<br /><br />But Venetia has no intention of losing her heart to the rakish lord until she is sure that beneath his swashbuckling ways and shocking manners lies a tender heart belonging to her. And Lord Damerel would marry her in a heartbeat if he did not think it would ruin her. Then she discovers a shocking family secret that changes everything ... It was therefore particularly provoking to find that occasion, Lord Damerel could make up his mind to be idiotically noble....</span>
  <a data-text-id="11965945163659195327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/610442-what-does-floored-by-the-hammer-mean">what does floored by the hammer mean?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_610442'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F32102.Venetia">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/610442-what-does-floored-by-the-hammer-mean">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/610442-what-does-floored-by-the-hammer-mean">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9225468-elizabeth"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1364960328i/9225468._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9225468-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It means floored by the auctioneer's hammer, Tattersall's is a major auctioneer of racehorses.<br/><br/>"I haven't yet been floored by the hammer, if that's wha<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It means floored by the auctioneer's hammer, Tattersall's is a major auctioneer of racehorses.<br /><br />"I haven't yet been floored by the hammer, if that's what you mean!"<br /><br />Venetia was asking whether he was in Yorkshire because of "that thing at Tattersall's"<br />I think Damerel was joking he's not yet in such dire financial circumstances that he's had to sell himself on the auction block. Venetia clarifies that by "that thing at Tattersalls" she means "Black Monday" or the "Settling Day"(the day after a big race when everyone has to settle their accounts) she's implying he's come back to his Yorkshire estate because he's lost a bunch of assets gambling, or sold all his racehorses.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_759394231" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759394231" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759394231?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=regency">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759394231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17697984338540903398">June 2019 reread with the Georgette Heyer group!<br/><br/>News flash: I'm not 18 any more. So even though I still have a soft spot for romances in general and Regencies in particular, my appetite for reading about sweet, silly young girls who do brainless things and have Big Misunderstandings with the guy has dwindled to almost zero. When you're yelling "TALK TO EACH OTHER, PEOPLE" at a book, it's not particularly conducive to the romantic feelz.<br/><br/>Which brings me to <i>Venetia</i>. Venetia herself is one of my fav</span>
  <span id="freeText17697984338540903398" style="display:none">June 2019 reread with the Georgette Heyer group!<br /><br />News flash: I'm not 18 any more. So even though I still have a soft spot for romances in general and Regencies in particular, my appetite for reading about sweet, silly young girls who do brainless things and have Big Misunderstandings with the guy has dwindled to almost zero. When you're yelling "TALK TO EACH OTHER, PEOPLE" at a book, it's not particularly conducive to the romantic feelz.<br /><br />Which brings me to <i>Venetia</i>. Venetia herself is one of my favorite Heyer heroines: intelligent, witty, resourceful and not easily fazed by events that would make most ladies throw up their hands in despair. She's 25 years old--just about on the shelf by Regency standards. Because her father was a damaged soul, Venetia has spent her entire life in a small town with a very limited circle of friends and acquaintances, but she's nevertheless well-read and socially adept, if rather innocent in the ways of the world.<br /><br />Enter Damerel: an older man who's a confirmed rake and pretty much doesn't care about anything any longer. Or at least he thinks he doesn't, but underneath there's an intelligent, kind man that his growing friendship with Venetia brings out of hiding. He starts out intending to seduce her--hey, she's a lovely girl and he's bored--but his growing friendship with and respect for her and her brother soon make him realize that he can't do that. Which leads to a moral conundrum for Damerel: his life has been <b>so</b> reprehensible that he's no longer accepted in society, and marrying a sweet younger lady like Venetia would make people despise him even more, and shun them both.<blockquote>"[I'm] something worse than a fool. <i>Would that she could make of me a saint, or I of her a sinner</i>-- For the first part it's too late, old friend, too late! And for the second--it was precisely my intention, and a rare moment this is to discover that if I could I would not!"</blockquote>What to do? The resolution isn't as simple as you might expect.<br /><br />It's lovely to watch Venetia's developing relationship with Damerel. They trade literary quotes and allusions and they just <i>understand</i> each other. Their relationship is in turns witty and heart-wrenching. And way sexier than any other Heyer romance I'm aware of! Heyer never gives you anything more than a kiss--no tangled tongues or groping or anything like that--but you can almost feel the heat rising off the pages when these two are together.<br /><br />I loved both the humor and the literary allusions and references in this book. I think it's the most intelligently written of the Heyer books I've read. I can feel my brain cells multiplying while I read it. Or expanding. Whatever it is they do. <br /><br />I found a handy online guide to the literary references in <i>Venetia</i>, which might help other readers too: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.heyerlist.org/notes/venetia/annotations.html">http://www.heyerlist.org/notes/veneti...</a>. This was invaluable in keeping my brain cells from exploding from trying to expand too fast.<br /><br />And I've changed my mind on this second read: <i>Venetia</i> gets all 5 stars.<br /><br />P.S. re "orgies": at the end of the book<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Damarel jokes that they're going to have a lovely orgy, or something to that effect. This has bothered a lot of readers, including me. But here's my evolved take on that scene: The first time I read that orgy comment I thought it was cynical; the second time I decided he and Venetia were just joking around. Then we were discussing it in our Georgette Heyer group read a few months ago, and someone said that what Damerel really means with that comment is that they're going to have a great wedding night and love life generally--a nice little "orgy" with just the two of them.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>I read the scene again and personally I'm convinced that that's the right interpretation. Hope that helps!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17697984338540903398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18003993616782657487" style="display:none"><i>Chapter 1</i>, in which I continue my love affair with a most enchanting author!<br /><br /><i>Chapter 2</i>, in which Venetia is established as a heroine of much wit, honesty, and vitality.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 3</i>, in which Venetia is contemplative of the rakish Lord Damerel and her brother Aubrey takes a wracking spill.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 4</i>, in which Venetia and Lord Damerel find the best of all things: friendship.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 5</i>, in which it is noted that the Scoundrel is but hidden twin to the Good Man: each male contains both sides; the Sensible Woman is best served by accepting that reality.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 6</i>, in which I return after a sojourn in Venice to Venetia, and find her just as charming as ever.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 7</i>, in which we enter the excruciatingly finite mind of Edward Yardley, suitor to Venetia.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 8</i>, in which we enter the intensely melodramatic mind of Oswald Denny, suitor to Venetia.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 9</i>, in which Venetia jumps from a loft, Oswald loses hold of his senses and showers her with kisses, Damerel adroitly dampens these boyish enthusiasms, and I smile from ear to ear.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 10</i>, in which Lady Denny realizes, aghast and agog, that true love beats in the hearts of sweet, innocent Venetia and that notorious rake, Damerel.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 11</i>, in which a frightful ogress enters the story!<br /><br /><i>Chapter 12</i>, in which the reader is reminded that a heroine's wit and virtues are often best illustrated when she is set against an ogress of the first order.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 13</i>, in which Damerel fiercely declares his love and Venetia is unperturbed by this statement of the obvious.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 14</i>, in which the reader recalls that allies with the best of intentions may be more obstinate and troublesome than the worst of enemies.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 15</i>, in which Venetia awakens into nightmare.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 16</i>, in which London fails to amuse or even distract.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 17</i>, in which Inspiration and Understanding strike like twin lightning bolts!<br /><br /><i>Chapter 18</i>, in which a shockingly exciting secret is revealed.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 19</i>, in which the shockingly exciting secret is met.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 20</i>, in which Venetia marshals her force of personality and wields her weapons of wit and earnestness in gentle battle against the <i>idiotish</i> and <i>stoopid</i> well-wishers surrounding her.<br /><br /><i>Chapter 21</i>, in a which a lady makes clear that she prefers a libertine and his orgies; and in which a perfect tale of quirky romance comes to a perfectly quirky romantic close.</span>

<div id="review_596363541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596363541" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18780551-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520389159p2/18780551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/18780551-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402238840" href="/book/show/10051392-venetia">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!!</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anne by: </span>
      Becca, Marquise, Seema, Tweety, QNPoohBear &amp; probably a whole lot of other people I forget!!!
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=dear-sir-i-am-in-love-with-you">dear-sir-i-am-in-love-with-you</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=georgette-heyer">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=tbr-challenge-2016">tbr-challenge-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=darling-books-i-want-to-hug">darling-books-i-want-to-hug</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=rakes">rakes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=love-heroine">love-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596363541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8915387770066039840">Yorkshire, 1818<br/><br/>*WARNING! Spoilers, gushing, swooning, quoting and rose-petal strewing ahead! ;) (no orgies though, I promise -- read on safely :P)*<br/><br/>O <i>Venetia</i>! Thou hast utterly captured my soul!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115401i/20683125._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>"A rose by any other name would smell as sweet."</i><br/><br/>And a Damerel by any other name would be just as swoon-worthy!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475115401ra/20683126.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>"I will be calm. I will be mistress of myself."</i><br/><br/>Because my name is Venetia and I'm one of the most wonderful heroines in all literature. I have lived one of the dreamiest romances possible, and have</span>
  <span id="freeText8915387770066039840" style="display:none">Yorkshire, 1818<br><br>*WARNING! Spoilers, gushing, swooning, quoting and rose-petal strewing ahead! ;) (no orgies though, I promise -- read on safely :P)*<br><br>O <i>Venetia</i>! Thou hast utterly captured my soul!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115401i/20683125._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"A rose by any other name would smell as sweet."</i><br><br>And a Damerel by any other name would be just as swoon-worthy!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475115401ra/20683126.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"I will be calm. I will be mistress of myself."</i><br><br>Because my name is Venetia and I'm one of the most wonderful heroines in all literature. I have lived one of the dreamiest romances possible, and have remained perfectly poised and ladylike through the whole thing, without seeming aloof or uninterested. I am simply awesome, that is all. I am sorry that no one else is ever going to have a romance as breathtakingly beautiful as mine. ;) <br><br><i>"I am determined that nothing but the deepest love could ever induce me into matrimony."</i><br><br>OK, Anne. I know <i>Venetia</i> has completely addled your brain, but there is no need to start quoting classic literature like some foolish bluestocking. You'll never be able to pull it off as swiftly as Damerel and Venetia. NOTHING COULD EVER COMPARE TO DAMEREL AND VENETIA. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475115401ra/20683127.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Yes, I know, I know, I use N&amp;S gifs WAY TOO MUCH. But I don't CARE. It's PERFECT here. #sorrynotsorry)<br><br>Quite simply, this book is exquisitely sublime. No amount of words to describe its peaceful, quiet beauty and entrancing depth would ever be sufficient. This is a masterpiece of the first order. Possibly Heyer's best novel in terms of perfectly blended substance and romanticism. I.Just.Love.It.<br><br>Everyone had been telling me to read this for <i>ages</i>. I knew I would love it, and was so excited to read it that a part of me did not want to read it too soon because...once you read it for the first time, you'll never read it again for the first time. Sure, re-reads are sometimes even better, but they're not the <i>same</i>. You already know just how swoony Damerel really is when you re-read it ;) <br><br><i>"Fair Fatality, you are the most unusual female I have encountered in all my thirty-eight years!"</i> (finally Anne is quoting the right book!)<br><br>In what is assuredly the most famous “first encounter” scene in all of Heyer’s books, a returning Lord Damerel looking devilishly handsome on his horse stumbles upon Venetia picking blackberries on his estate grounds, and immediately just starts throwing out quotes and kissing her ruthlessly, you know, like any normal landlord would do. And Venetia? <i>She quotes back</i>. I kid you not, this girl may be inexperienced, but she knows what’s up. You want to act like a cad? Well so be it. <br><br><i>"'[y]our quotations don’t make your advances a whit more acceptable to me – and they don’t deceive me into thinking you anything but a <b>pestilent complete knave!</b>'"</i><br><br>And Damerel is all OH MY GOSH, SHE QUOTES BACK. SHE UNDERSTANDS. SHE’S THE ONE. <br><br>Thus it begins, my friends. One of the most beautiful romances I’ve ever read, solidly grounded on friendship, mutual understanding, and true love. <br><br><i>”’Or don’t you know how beautiful you are?’<br>‘Yes,’ replied Venetia, taking the wind out of his sails. <b>’Item, two lips, indifferent red – ‘ </b><br>‘Oh no, you’re quite out, and have gone to the wrong poet besides! <b>They look like rosebuds filled with snow!’</b>”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115586i/20683146._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aren’t they something??! What I wouldn’t give for such an encounter when I go blackberry-picking! Maybe I should try trespassing on some hot guy’s property? ;) <br><br>From that first meeting it is obvious that Damerel and Venetia are kindred spirits, and that probably no one else will understand them. Venetia may be “on the shelf”, sheltered in the country, inexperienced and optimistic, but she ain’t dumb. She’s not a chit who can’t tell love apart from attraction, or who is likely to have her head turned just because some swoony hot lord quotes poetry to her and calls her his “dear delight”. No. She falls for Damerel because he’s her soulmate, and she has sense enough to recognize that. Never mind that he’s the rakest rake in England, with a shocking past of wild orgies and seducing married women, or that he’s up to his eyeballs in debts. WHO CARES. VENETIA HAS FOUND A FRIEND. A <i>real</i> friend.<br><br>And no one understands. No one gets it. They all think Venetia is going to have her heart broken, that she doesn’t understand what Damerel is up to, that she’s too good and innocent to be with him. They warn her and counsel her and beg her to stay away from him, yet they never once ask her what she feels or what she thinks about him. <br><br>If only they knew how alike they are, and what good jokes they share. “OMG YOU’VE JUST HAD THE MOST DIVERTING THOUGHT??!!?!”<br><br>Their only ally is Venetia’s hilarious younger brother Aubrey, a smart and sassy scholarly boy who prefers books to people (see? People who prefer books usually understand people better! We <i>know</i>), and who had wonderfully good scenes and witty lines as sharp as rapiers.<br>The first part of the book passes by quietly, with autumn settling in and Damerel and Venetia being wrapped up in each other, being the best of friends and accomplices. Damerel takes to calling Venetia his “dear delight”, his “fair fatality”, “Admir'd Venetia” and other similar heart-melting nicknames, he keeps telling her she is a beautiful, desirable creature, and that he wouldn’t at all mind kissing her again, and well everything is just so sigh-worthy that you never want it to end.<br><br><i>”’[…]he should have taken you in his arms, like this, and not as though he were a bear, bent on hugging you to death. Nor am I in favour of dabbing kisses all over a girl’s face. If you cannot persuade her, by a ruse, to look up, you should make her do so, with a hand under her chin – thus, my dear delight!’”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115586i/20683147._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>BUT THEN, MRS. SCORRIER ENTERS THE PICTURE AND UTTERLY RUINS EVERYTHING. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475115726ra/20683166.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She meddles, she disturbs everything at Undershaw, she insults Venetia, and she drives everybody batty. I will be honest, the bits about her and her interference in the house were pretty boring, and maybe a bit too long, but mostly, they were infuriating. She was intolerable. <br><br>But her arrival is also a catalyst that strikes up a series of unforeseen twists and turns, and the second half of the book is definitely more fast-paced and surprising than the first. <br><br>Having been pushed to her limits by Mrs. S., Venetia declares her intention of setting up house in London, which unwittingly prompts Damerel into a most moving love declaration, although interrupted by Aubrey (Aubrey interruption # 1 of about 5000!!), but that leaves you swooning nonetheless.<br><br><i>”’You call me your friend, but I never called you mine, and never shall! You remained, and always will, <b>a beautiful, desirable creature</b>!’”</i><br><br>Ooooh if only Aubrey hadn’t come in at that moment! And if Venetia’s uncle had never come to Yorkshire! How things would have been different! <br><br>But as it is, the aforementioned people DID meddle, and in one of the most poignant, heart-breaking scenes I’ve ever read in any romance novel, Damerel <b>suddenly decides to act like the noblest of noble knights</b>, and in so doing breaks Venetia’s heart (and mine!) and his own. <br><br><i>”’Well – thus ends a charming autumn idyll, eh?’”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115726i/20683167.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just need to give Venetia a big hug. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475115726ra/20683168.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was so SHOCKED, so SPEECHLESS when I read that, that I basically dropped my book and sat there gaping for ages. <br><br>OH DAMEREL YOU INFURIATING DARLING. HOW COULD YOU!!!<br><br>Poor Venetia goes to London with her heart sunk to the lowest depths of despair, but still she’s no fool, and knows something must have happened to make Damerel suddenly change his mind when she had been so sure of his love. She just doesn’t know what. <br><br>But oh, when she finds out…oh, when she finds out, Damerel better WATCH IT. Oh, she ain’t gonna let him get away with his darned newfound chilvalry, OH HECK NO! <br><br>HE BETTER START STREWING THOSE BLASTED ROSE PETALS!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115931i/20683190._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>ALL THE WAY TO YORKSHIRE!<br><br><b>
  <u>Venetia:</u>
</b> *bursts into Damerel’s dining room while he is quietly intoxicating himself*<br><b>
  <u>Damerel:</u>
</b> OH GOD, NO!!! (this is the actual line!! :P :P)<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: OH GOD, YES!! Why do you have to be drunk just <i>now</i>??<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: ASJFKJLKJLK VENETIA!!! VENETIA, IT’S VENETIA! VEEEEEENEEEEETIIIIIAAAAAAA!!!!<br>*passionate-kissing-fond-embraces-insert-disgusting-sounds-here*<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: * reluctantly pulling away* Ohhhhh why did you come back??! Noooo!! I can’t DO THIS!!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: I need money to pay the driver, do you have your purse?<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Venetia, noooo, you weren’t supposed to come back, you can’t – I can’t – ARGH!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Please, your purse, I really need to pay my driver!<br><b>
  <u>Imber</u>
</b>: *quietly coming in* Uuuhhhh….miss? You don’t mean to stay <i>here</i> do you?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh hell yes I am staying HERE! I have been anxiously traveling all day long just to get here, and now you think I’d go away? Uh-uh!!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: NOOOOOOO!!!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: YEEESSSSSS! AND I AM STARVING, SO PLEASE GET ME SOME FOOD!!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Venetia, please no, YOU CAN’T!!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, I see, you have decided to be idiotish again, is that it???<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Awww “idiotish” *sniff* I never though I would hear you say that again!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, I didn’t even notice I said it a lot! Must be quite a number of idiotish people in my life, LOL!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Lol!! But….you can’t stay here!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, come on, don’t start again, if you kick me out of your house, I am building me a cabin outside, and will probably die of an inflammation of the lungs, and it will be all your fault!<br><b>
  <u>Marston</u>
</b>: Heyyy, Venetia!! Good to see you!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Hey, you too! But Damerel here isn’t happy to see me at all and threatens to kick me out!<br><b>
  <u>Marston</u>
</b>: No, what a jerk! Here, come upstairs with me.<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: NOOOOOOOOOO!!!!<br>***<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Alright, so, I have an idea, since you refuse to leave, I'LL leave and go to the inn, that way proprieties will be respected, and isn't that nice? I love proprieties :) And I love how you do your hair now! Very pretty!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: (Oooh man, is he ever difficult!) Well thank you!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: A la Sappho it's called right?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh you wretch, do you know the names of all the types of coiffures??!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Yup, pretty much! So, really now, what brought you here?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Well duuuhhh, the mail-coach of course!!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Don't sass me you little vixen! OHHHH WHY DID YOU COME!!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: (Ohhhh boy, here he goes again!) Why don't you just kiss me again and stop acting like such a stoopid??!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: NO! I DO NOT WANT TO KISS YOU! I WAS DRUNK, DARN IT!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Aahhh never mind! My food has arrived :D :D<br>***<br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: Oh thank goodness I arrived just in time! Venetia! What the heck is this I hear about you wanting Damerel to strew rose petals all over for you?<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Hahahahaha!! At <i>this</i> season??? <br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, shut up Damerel! You should've done it a long time ago, so hush!<br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: Or maybe she just didn't want you to indulge in such wasteful habits? I mean, who wastes rose petals like that???!!! But anyways that's NOT the point, the point is, I am here to prevent you from ruining yourself, Venetia!!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Yes!!! I second the motion!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: *major eye roll* HOW ABOUT I TELL Y'ALL WHAT I WANT!! There is no need to overreact! Damerel may be a little older than me, but at least he won't turn out to be my father! ;) <br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: WHAT??!!!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: HAHAHAHAHAHAAAAAAA OEDIPUS!!! But it's the other way around honey, YOU won't turn out to be MY mother!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, same thing! Be quiet!<br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: Geeee...I don't understand anything! Venetia, you seem to be living in a - in a, a....<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Soap-bubble?<br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: Yes!! Exactly! A soap-bubble!! Girl, WHAT IS GOING ON??<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Lol, if you think that I think Damerel is a fairytale hero, don't worry, I know he isn't! <br><b>
  <u>Mr. Hendred</u>
</b>: Ooooh Venetia, you don't understand! Damerel is a man of the world! He won't be able to reform all his shocking habits just for you! You will be made dreadfully unhappy!<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: *eyes glinting* Well, my love?<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: *eyes glinting back* Well, my dear delight?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: You'll continue to have orgies?<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: What if I do? What will you do?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Oh, I won't mind! I'll just...head up to bed or something!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Oh. Wouldn't you want to...participate, maybe?<br><b>
  <u>Venetia</u>
</b>: Welll....do you think I'd enjoy myself? ;) ;) ;) <br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: OH YOU SHALL HAVE A SPLENDID ORGY JUST FOR YOU, MY DEAREST OF DEAR DELIGHTS!!!<br><b>
  <u>Aubrey</u>
</b>: *interrupting for the 5000th time* Heeeyyyy just wanted to ask, but...can we go to Greece for you guys' honeymoon??<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: There won't be a honeymoon, because there won't be a wedding, because there hasn't been a proposal yet, BECAUSE YOU KEEP INTERRUPTING!!<br><b>
  <u>Aubrey</u>
</b>: Oh. Well, when you <i>finally</i> propose, can we go to Greece?<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: In the middle of winter? You mad?<br><b>
  <u>Aubrey</u>
</b>: Well okay, then it had better be Rome. I would have preferred Greece, but we can go to Rome, and I think Venetia will like it. It's not <i>my</i> honeymoon after all!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: Just. Get. To. Bed.<br><b>
  <u>Aubrey</u>
</b>: Right! The proposal! Goodnight!<br><b>
  <u>Damerel</u>
</b>: FINALLY!!! PROPOSAL TIME!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475115401i/20683128._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"'O God, I love you to the edge of madness Venetia!'"</i><br><br>Yes, I really do love you to the edge of madness, <i>Venetia</i>. This is undoubtedly one of my favourite books of all times. I want to buy a whole cart-full and walk around campus handing a copy to everybody. "Read this, it will make you feel better. Read this, it is simply phenomenal. READ IT, I SAY!!"<br><br>I could go on and on about this book for ages, but this review is already almost two months late, and no one probably even remembers that I read it. I am so sorry I took ages to write this review (again)! You can blame my addled brain. ;) <br><br>Buddy-read with Becca!! :D <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8915387770066039840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2703677461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2703677461" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505852430p2/68708752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2703677461?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2703677461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13728942598993081557">This is a sweet little historical romance with a hero and heroine who are like minded in being, smart, witty and refreshingly honest with each other. Unlike most of this genre, the virginal lady knows exactly who the rake is and loves him anyway, because she can see that beneath the veneer of ugly behavior is a kind man. <br/><br/>She, Venetia (ugly name and how is it pronounced?), has seen his kindness in action when her younger brother, Aubrey, who has a lame leg, is injured horse riding near the gentle</span>
  <span id="freeText13728942598993081557" style="display:none">This is a sweet little historical romance with a hero and heroine who are like minded in being, smart, witty and refreshingly honest with each other. Unlike most of this genre, the virginal lady knows exactly who the rake is and loves him anyway, because she can see that beneath the veneer of ugly behavior is a kind man. <br /><br />She, Venetia (ugly name and how is it pronounced?), has seen his kindness in action when her younger brother, Aubrey, who has a lame leg, is injured horse riding near the gentleman's estate and Damerel takes him home to recover. While there, Aubrey is handled beautifully by Damerel who instinctively realizes that the boy hates pity and truly despises being treated like an invalid. The character of Aubrey is wonderful and I soon grew to love him just as much as his sister does. Aubrey is a brilliant scholar and also has a rapier wit like Venetia and although quite acerbic and self-involved, truly loves his sister and wants her to be happy.<br /><br />All's well that ends well and there are some skeletons in everyone's closet that make this love match, not nearly as unequal as we are led to believe in the beginning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13728942598993081557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Melindam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melindam" href="/user/show/36434323-melindam">Melindam</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6408511774902892308">Enjoyed the story very much. Venetia's sense, sass and humour is nothing short of amazing. <br/><br/>The hero was cut out along the usual lines of generic, worldweary, byronic rake and I found him quite meh, but I got used to him in the end.</span>

<div id="review_718606393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/718606393" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373481234p2/4784586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/718606393?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781843793793" href="/book/show/7124226-venetia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=loved-the-hero">loved-the-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=loved-the-heroine">loved-the-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer718606393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6932338437968440858">Here's the thing: This book is one of my all-time favorite books. I've read it so many times by now that I lost count. And yet I never wrote a review, because I could never really find the right words to do this book justice. When I <i>finally</i> convinced two of my good friends to give this book a try, yet another re-read was in order! And guess what, I still love it, and still can't come up with coherent reasons why. <br/><br/>Let's start with the heroine:<br/><i>"I wish you will tell me some of the things you have d</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6932338437968440858" style="display:none">Here's the thing: This book is one of my all-time favorite books. I've read it so many times by now that I lost count. And yet I never wrote a review, because I could never really find the right words to do this book justice. When I <i>finally</i> convinced two of my good friends to give this book a try, yet another re-read was in order! And guess what, I still love it, and still can't come up with coherent reasons why. <br /><br />Let's start with the heroine:<br /><i>"I wish you will tell me some of the things you have done!" "I think not," he said dryly. "I said some of the things you have done!" she exclaimed indignantly. "You can't have spent your whole life getting into idiotish scrapes!" The ugly look vanished as he burst out laughing. "Most of it, I assure you!"</i><br /><br />I ADORE Venetia. She is one of the most sensible, level-headed, determined and yet completely loveable heroines I have ever had the pleasure to read about. Whatever life throws at her (and boy does it throw things at her: a terrible, egotistical father who pretty much buries her alive on his secluded country estate, the egotistical brothers who never think about her happiness, the self-centered aunt who doesn't do anything to help alleviate her situation, to name only a few), she somehow remains cheerful and optimistic, never gives up, and always finds a way to be happy with what she has. I truly envy her in that respect. I love how she never tries to change Damerel, how she sees him for exactly what he is, and loves him for all his bad parts together. <br /><br />Then there's our darling rake, Jasper, Lord Damerel:<br /><i>"Fair Fatality, you are the most unusual female I have ever encountered in all my thirty-eight years!" "You can't think how deeply flattered I am!" she assured him. "I daresay my head would be quite turned if I didn't suspect that amongst so many a dozen or so may have slipped from your memory." "More like a hundred. Am I never to learn your name?"</i><br /><br />I LOVE this man. He comes such a long way in this book, and not because someone forces him to change, but because meeting an innocent little whirlwind who turns his life of debauchery upside down actually makes him re-evaluate his life-choices and accept that he has screwed up and he is not good enough for her as he is. He's no angel, and I love him even more for that. He hasn't been a good landowner or anything, but he does try his best to become one.<br />I absolutely love his sense of humor! I wish I had someone to trade Shakespearean insults with in everyday conversation... <br /><br />Which brings me to: the most delicious banter! <br /><i>"I can't come down that ladder while you stand there watching me." "Can't you? Oh, that's easily remedied!" he retorted, and removed the ladder. It was this impish action which drew the protest from her which Oswald heard. "Fiend!" She said. "Do put it back, and go away!" "Not I!" he replied, grinning up at her. "But it is most unchivalrous of you!" "No, no. On the contrary. The ladder is clearly unsafe."</i><br /> <br />Oh, the banter. Be still my heart &lt;3 These two are truly equals, if not in education or anything else, but definitely when it comes to wit and humor. They love teasing one another, try to find the most obscure poetry reference to quote and see if the other one recognizes it... I love every moment of it! <br /><br />Last, and MOST IMPORTANTLY, the narration:<br />Oh sweet mercy, the heavenly narration &lt;3 Richard Armitage is one of my favorite actors and narrators! He has such a beautiful voice, it's just a delight to listen to. No matter how long the book, he always finds a unique voice for each character that helps you identify who is speaking at every moment without a clue from the text. Even his female characters sounds believable! It's just tremendous fun to listen to him bring a book to live! If you don't believe me, see Becca's review below: he managed to get a complete audiobook hater to admit that this is perfection! At this point I have actually listened to this book more often than I have read it, and trust me, if you hear the man's voice, you'll understand why... <br />Sadly, this is an abridged version which cut some of my favorite moments, but this in no way dims my love for this production! <br /><br />There is a reason this is the book I turn to whenever I'm in a slump, or just need a pick-me-up. I love the characters, their determination, the heart and humor, and all of it together makes for one perfect reading experience. If you have never read a Georgette Heyer book, I cannot recommend this highly enough as a starting point!!!<br /><br />Also, here are the reviews of the two friends I convinced to try this (they both loved it, so YAY):<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373857215" rel="nofollow noopener">Lacey's review</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385509132" rel="nofollow noopener">Becca's review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6932338437968440858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_266728782" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266728782" />
    <a title="Dawn (&amp; Ron)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2447325-dawn-ron"><img alt="Dawn (&amp; Ron)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336267796p2/2447325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266728782?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn (&amp; Ron)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn (&amp; Ron)" href="/user/show/2447325-dawn-ron">Dawn (&amp; Ron)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11432520-venetia">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jane Austen and Regency fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=tbr-challenge">tbr-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=regency">regency</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=kindle-read">kindle-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2447325-dawn-ron?shelf=stretching-reading-horizon">stretching-reading-horizon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266728782" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15460713373008742373">I am one of those who steered clear of Georgette Heyer for years, even though I heard the comparisons to Jane Austen, I was afraid they were formulaic romances. To my surprise it wasn't what I feared all those years and proved that breaking out of one's reading comfort zone can be quite rewarding. This was made more enjoyable getting to read this along with Sabrina, who also had some of the same feelings regarding Heyer, and both of us ended up enjoying it. <br/><br/>I was aware Heyer was famous, or some </span>
  <span id="freeText15460713373008742373" style="display:none">I am one of those who steered clear of Georgette Heyer for years, even though I heard the comparisons to Jane Austen, I was afraid they were formulaic romances. To my surprise it wasn't what I feared all those years and proved that breaking out of one's reading comfort zone can be quite rewarding. This was made more enjoyable getting to read this along with Sabrina, who also had some of the same feelings regarding Heyer, and both of us ended up enjoying it. <br /><br />I was aware Heyer was famous, or some may say infamous, for her Regency cant. I admit to being a bit intimidated with the thought of tackling this period slang, did you know there are about 30 words just for dimwitted? So, to prepare I bookmarked several websites and had the book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7936036.Georgette_Heyer_s_Regency_World" title="Georgette Heyer's Regency World by Jennifer Kloester" rel="nofollow noopener">Georgette Heyer's Regency World</a>, at the ready. At first it was a little difficult and distracting trying to figure out the meaning, but the patient help I received from fellow GR friends was invaluable. Their input made it much more fun, allowing me to relax, stop worrying and make it more of a game instead. <br /> Our heroine, Venetia, <i>"then twenty-two, perilously near to being on the shelf."</i> is quite modern not only for the Regency period but for the 1950's, when this was originally written. She is unconventional with her free thoughts and expressions but at the same time not challenging her family to take care of their responsibilities. I did find her conveniently too naive at times for purposes of the story. Then we have our hero Damarel, that dastardly bad boy and rake, or using Regency cant a rip. He doesn't hide who he is or his past from Venetia, even using his reputation to his advantage at times. As he finds himself falling for Venetia he wins over the reader too. How can one resist lines like this -<br /><br /><blockquote>What I regret I can never undo, for the gods don’t annihilate space, or time, or transform such a man as I am into one worthy to be your husband.<br /></blockquote><br /><br />The accolades for Heyer's historical detail are justified. Daily life, settings, clothing and manners are richly painted, giving a clear picture of the genteel, decorous yet rigid Regency society. She also presents the limited expectations for women in an unapologetic yet realistic way. Everything is laced with wit and humor. <br /><br /><blockquote>"...my case is clearly past remedy, and I've nothing to do but decide whether to be an aunt to Conway's children, or a mother to Edward's - and I have a lowering presentiment that Edward's children will be dreadfully dull, poor little things!"</blockquote><br /><br />There are no cardboard cutout characters, they are multi-layered, full of life whether you hate them, love them, laugh at them or barely tolerate them. Venetia's suitors, or men in waiting, as I came to think of them, Edward Yardley and Oswald Denny, had me laughing with their pursuit and dreams of gallantry. I grew to appreciate Aubrey, her younger brother, and how he coped with being lame in a time when such imperfections were unacceptable, shunned and shamed by many. <br /><br /><blockquote>"Master Aubrey’s hatred of his disability, and his passionate desire to show himself as hearty and as independent as his more fortunate contemporaries:</blockquote><br /><br />Heyer cleverly puts all these people together, some we never even meet, some we only briefly meet and some we never expect to meet, yet they are all important to putting the final picture together. <br /><br />There is no surprise about how things will end, the fun is how they get to happily ever after, including an expected twist I didn't see coming. I loved the endearments they called each other, she called him "The Wicked Baron" and he called her "My Dear Delight". This was my first brush with Heyer and I don't plan on it being my last. Will I judge all her others against this one? I hope not, but Damarel will be hard to top, so only time will tell. On that note I'll let Damarel end this review and prove why he is not easily forgotten.<br /><br /><blockquote>"When you smile at me like that, it’s all holiday with me!"</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15460713373008742373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_423330130" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423330130" />
    <a title="Rebecca May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11349024-rebecca-may"><img alt="Rebecca May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531472983p2/11349024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423330130?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca May" href="/user/show/11349024-rebecca-may">Rebecca May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402238840" href="/book/show/10051392-venetia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11349024-rebecca-may?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423330130" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14659556437183270076">Never in my life have I been so glad of a rainy afternoon. Never so glad that I was bored and typed a name into a search bar to see what would come up. <br/><br/>It was in this slightly unorthodox way that I originally discovered <i>Venetia</i>. In a fit of utter boredom I typed the name “Richard Armitage” (he'd recently become my favourite actor) into the iTunes search bar, and what should appear? ...Three novels by Georgette Heyer, narrated by Richard Armitage. <br/><br/>I need not tell you I was wide awake again after </span>
  <span id="freeText14659556437183270076" style="display:none">Never in my life have I been so glad of a rainy afternoon. Never so glad that I was bored and typed a name into a search bar to see what would come up. <br><br>It was in this slightly unorthodox way that I originally discovered <i>Venetia</i>. In a fit of utter boredom I typed the name “Richard Armitage” (he'd recently become my favourite actor) into the iTunes search bar, and what should appear? ...Three novels by Georgette Heyer, narrated by Richard Armitage. <br><br>I need not tell you I was wide awake again after that. Before then a few friends had vaguely recommended Georgette Heyer’s novels to me, but thus far I had lacked the motivation to start finding and reading them. The summaries made them sound to me as if there was nothing much out of the ordinary about them. How wrong could I have been? I absolutely loved <i>Venetia</i>, and I will be endlessly grateful to Richard Armitage for being my unwitting introduction to Georgette Heyer's beautiful world.<br><br>Being set in the Yorkshire countryside, the story doesn’t have quite so many upsets and excitements and scrapes of those Heyer stories which take place in the cities. Those stories can be amazingly good fun, and very exciting. But while <i>Venetia</i> lacks those particular excitements, it does have a quiet beauty to it, a serenity and gentle humour that lends it an equal merit to the other more riotous novels, and indeed it is superior to some. I suppose it really depends on what you’re in the mood for, and if you’re in the mood for a unique romance set in the English countryside, this novel is utterly perfect. Besides, <i>Venetia</i> was my first Georgette Heyer novel (not to mention my first Richard-Armitage-narrated novel), and therefore is very dear to me, occupying a small but precious space in my heart.<br><br>Miss Venetia Lanyon is one of Georgette Heyer’s slightly older heroines, a young woman who has lived in the countryside for most of her twenty-five years, ever since her mother died when she was a young girl. Her brother Conway has escaped into the wider world by joining the army, and in wilfully and obstinately choosing to remain abroad, he has left the control of the Undershore estate in Venetia’s hands. She has grown to have a kind heart, a brilliant sense of humour, and a taste for adventure. But this sensible girl and stunning beauty can see no choices before her save to be an ageing spinster in her brother’s household, or a wife to one Edward Yardley and the mother of his children... until she chances across Lord Damarel, the “Wicked Baron”. <br><br>Though I find it hard to approve of Lord Damarel’s mode of entering the story, like Venetia I was quickly enamoured of him. In the past he has been – we are told – prone to taking one mistress after the other, and engaging in any number of scandalous pursuits. Unfortunately for him, scandalous pursuits tend to be somewhat expensive, and as such he is forced to return to his country estate to “ruralise”, at which point he encounters the lovely Venetia Lanyon. <br><br>From this point on we are treated to delightful, witty exchanges between the two characters. Their habit of constantly quoting poetry at each other means that the reader can very quickly feel the rapport form between them, as circumstances conspire to throw them together and become the best of friends. Best of all, they understand one another. <br><br>I think what I love about these two characters is that Venetia and Damarel are on very even terms with each other, more so than in any other Heyer novel I’ve ever read. There is no feeling that one, by virtue of experience or age or intelligence, is superior to the other. Of course Lord Damarel has seen a great deal more of the world than Venetia, but as their intellects are equally sharp, this circumstance gives rise to more amusement between them than trouble. Their relationship is certainly one of my favourite romances. With every passing moment that they talk and laugh and discuss things together, you feel more and more certain that these two people were simply made for each other. It’s a lovely thing to behold.<br><br>Before Damarel even enters the story, however, we meet his rivals – Oswald, the nineteen year old neighbour to Venetia, and Edward, the man who has for several years considered himself as good as engaged to Venetia, despite having been refused by Venetia and despite the fact that he is not particularly in love with her. To give you an idea of the relative personalities of these contenders for Venetia’s hand, I’ve attempted to represent my reaction to them:<br><br>~ <b>When Oswald walks into the room:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384905229ra/7024130.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~ <b>When Edward walks into the room:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425555420ra/13904870.gif" width="372" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>~ <b>When Lord Damarel walks into the room:</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425555420ra/13904871.gif" width="327" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Seriously, ladies. You won’t know what hit you.<br><br>~ <b>When a man walks into the room, who you think is Damarel and it turns out to be Edward:</b> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460209104ra/18713470.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The disappointment is indescribable. <br><br>Oswald, for his part, is seen by Venetia as too young – at nineteen - to be seriously in love. I think Heyer is playing with a bit of a dangerous double-standard here, as quite a few of her own heroines have been as young as Oswald, even two or three years younger. I do however understand that being able to love rather depends on one’s personal emotional maturity, and by that standard Oswald is certainly far too “young” to be seriously in love with Venetia. Certainly the reader is never under any apprehension that he is a serious rival for Venetia’s affections, and in fact his exploits can be extremely amusing.<br><br>Edward, on the other hand, I just want to strangle. He’s the sort of man that is not necessarily stupid or mean or selfish... but with every word that comes out of his mouth you become more and more desperate for a convenient wall to bang your head against to alleviate the boredom and frustration. Or a convenient swing on which to swing around and around in circles... either one will do. He is unbelievably stuffy and patronising, and his arrogance is the more irritating because he isn’t really aware of how arrogant he is. His impertinence extends so far as to try and joke with Venetia and pretend he’s “gone a trifle deaf” when she tells him in no uncertain terms that she will not marry him. (Cue glaring, clenching of fists and stifled screams of frustration - Edward Yardley is honestly so annoying!!)<br><br>He is not, however, the only one causing trouble for Venetia and Damarel. Damarel's morally chequered past certainly doesn't help matters, and to replace the upsets and excitements of the city, this novel is so full of meddlers! So many people are utterly convinced they know what is best for Venetia, and have little intention of consulting her before deciding what to do with her life. It is these people that cause the most trouble for the couple. The one glorious exception is Venetia’s younger brother. <br><br>Aubrey was certainly not intended as a hero, but in some inexplicable way I found myself falling in love with him almost as much as I was falling for Damarel. Aubrey is seventeen, wonderfully intelligent, entertainingly precocious, and rather touchy about the fact that he walks with a limp, due to a disease that affected his hip joint when he was younger. He enjoys the company of books more than he does most people – save Lord Damarel - and though he can be egotistical and unwittingly selfish, Aubrey will often surprise you by showing the depth of genuine feeling he has for his sister, which is truly touching. He's a difficult character to describe, but anyone who has read about him should understand my fondness for him.<br><br>Readers of Heyer's novels will know that they are filled with sparkling wit and exciting twists. Then too, there is always at least one scene where she really uses her writing ability to its utmost and can emotionally destroy the reader in a single chapter. Of course I didn’t know of her habit of doing this when I first read <i>Venetia</i>. However, even after a year of reading some of her other novels, I truly believe this particular scene in <i>Venetia</i> is one of the best she has written. It brings me to tears every single time… and here I must put in a word of praise for Richard Armitage’s narration. His narration is always more than delightful, of course, but here he really comes into his own. The way his tone changes to reflect the complete, heart-breaking sadness is perfect. His voice reflects every nuance of feeling in the scene, and it makes the moment even more powerful.<br><br>The audio edition is somewhat abridged, something I was actually grateful for in this case. The original novel can occasionally get slightly bogged down in extraneous detail… and though I don’t generally consider myself a prude, the word “orgy” was used in the final chapter perhaps one too many times for my liking… I believe it was three times in a single page? In any case, I have another reason to be glad of that part being left out of the audio edition. If I had heard Richard Armitage say that word so many times in such quick succession, I believe I probably would have ended up blushing and/or giggling for the better part of a week. Those who know me well know that isn’t quite as much of an exaggeration as it may seem.<br><br>In all seriousness, however… inappropriate words aside, <i>Venetia</i> will always be one of my favourite Georgette Heyer novels, and Venetia and Damarel one of my favourite couples. The two of them – and Venetia’s brilliant younger brother – kept me constantly feeling as if I were on the edge of delighted laughter. If you are looking for a wild romp through the Regency world with sword-fights and carriage chases and what have you, this wouldn’t do for you at all. Pick up another Heyer, there are plenty to choose from. But if you are looking for a quiet, wonderful, beautiful novel, <i>Venetia</i> is perfect. If you can listen to Richard Armitage read it to you? So much the better. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14659556437183270076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2383718157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2383718157" />
    <a title="Andrea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea"><img alt="Andrea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373481234p2/4784586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2383718157?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrea" href="/user/show/4784586-andrea">Andrea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402238840" href="/book/show/10051392-venetia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=loved-the-hero">loved-the-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4784586-andrea?shelf=loved-the-heroine">loved-the-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2383718157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15427709554788119310">Here's the thing: This book is one of my all-time favorite books. I've read it so many times by now that I lost count. And yet I never wrote a review, because I could never really find the right words to do this book justice. When I <i>finally</i> convinced to of my good friends to give this book a try, yet another re-read was in order! And guess what, I still love it, and still can't come up with coherent reasons why. <br/><br/>Let's start with the heroine:<br/><i>"I wish you will tell me some of the things you have do</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15427709554788119310" style="display:none">Here's the thing: This book is one of my all-time favorite books. I've read it so many times by now that I lost count. And yet I never wrote a review, because I could never really find the right words to do this book justice. When I <i>finally</i> convinced to of my good friends to give this book a try, yet another re-read was in order! And guess what, I still love it, and still can't come up with coherent reasons why. <br /><br />Let's start with the heroine:<br /><i>"I wish you will tell me some of the things you have done!" "I think not," he said dryly. "I said some of the things you have done!" she exclaimed indignantly. "You can't have spent your whole life getting into idiotish scrapes!" The ugly look vanished as he burst out laughing. "Most of it, I assure you!"</i><br /><br />I ADORE Venetia. She is one of the most sensible, level-headed, determined and yet completely loveable heroines I have ever had the pleasure to read about. Whatever life throws at her (and boy does it throw things at her: a terrible, egotistical father who pretty much buries her alive on his secluded country estate, the egotistical brothers who never think about her happiness, the self-centered aunt who doesn't do anything to help alleviate her situation, to name only a few), she somehow remains cheerful and optimistic, never gives up, and always finds a way to be happy with what she has. I truly envy her in that respect. I love how she never tries to change Damerel, how she sees him for exactly what he is, and loves him for all his bad parts together. <br /><br />Then there's our darling rake, Jasper, Lord Damerel:<br /><i>"Fair Fatality, you are the most unusual female I have ever encountered in all my thirty-eight years!" "You can't think how deeply flattered I am!" she assured him. "I daresay my head would be quite turned if I didn't suspect that amongst so many a dozen or so may have slipped from your memory." "More like a hundred. Am I never to learn your name?"</i><br /><br />I LOVE this man. He comes such a long way in this book, and not because someone forces him to change, but because meeting an innocent little whirlwind who turns his life of debauchery upside down actually makes him re-evaluate his life-choices and accept that he has screwed up and he is not good enough for her as he is. He's no angel, and I love him even more for that. He hasn't been a good landowner or anything, but he does try his best to become one.<br />I absolutely love his sense of humor! I wish I had someone to trade Shakespearean insults with in everyday conversation... <br /><br />Which brings me to: the most delicious banter! <br /><i>"I can't come down that ladder while you stand there watching me." "Can't you? Oh, that's easily remedied!" he retorted, and removed the ladder. It was this impish action which drew the protest from her which Oswald heard. "Fiend!" She said. "Do put it back, and go away!" "Not I!" he replied, grinning up at her. "But it is most unchivalrous of you!" "No, no. On the contrary. The ladder is clearly unsafe."</i><br /> <br />Oh, the banter. Be still my heart &lt;3 These two are truly equals, if not in education or anything else, but when it comes to wit and humor. They love teasing one another, try to find the most obscure poetry reference to quote and see if the other one recognizes it... I love every moment of it! <br /><br />This is their relationship in a nutshell: <br />"As soon as one promises not to do something it becomes the one thing above all others that one most wishes to do!" She turned her head towards her uncle again. "You mean to warn me that he may continue to have mistresses, and orgies, and- and so-on, don't you, sir?" "Particularly so-on!" interpolated Damerel. "Well, how should I know all the shocking things you do? The thing is, uncle, that I don't think I ever should know." "You'd know about my orgies!" objected Damerel. "Yes, but I shouldn't care about them, once in a while. After all, it would be quite unreasonable to wish you to change all your habits, and I can always retire to bed, can't I?" "Oh, you won't preside over them?" he said, much disappointed. "Yes, love, if you wish me to," she replied, smiling at him. "Should I enjoy them?" He stretched out his hand, and when she laid her own in it, held it very tightly. "You shall have a splendid orgy, my dear delight, and you will enjoy it very much indeed!"<br /><br />There is a reason this is the book I turn to whenever I'm in a slump, or just need a pick-me-up. I love the characters, their determination, the heart and humor, and all of it together makes for one perfect reading experience. If you have never read a Georgette Heyer book, I cannot recommend this highly enough as a starting point!!!<br /><br />Also, here are the reviews of the two friends I convinced to try this (they both loved it, so YAY):<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373857215" rel="nofollow noopener">Lacey's review</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385509132" rel="nofollow noopener">Becca's review</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15427709554788119310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
