<div id="review_2385509132" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385509132" />
    <a title="Becca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15807787-becca"><img alt="Becca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398883325p2/15807787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385509132?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becca" href="/user/show/15807787-becca">Becca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781843793793" href="/book/show/7124226-venetia">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15807787-becca?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15807787-becca?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385509132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7977266432489578084">This was my first audiobook AND my first Georgette Heyer! I know...it's a bit disgraceful that I've waited this long to read a book from the woman whom many consider to be the creator of the Regency romance, but while I love Jane Austen and other not-modern authors, I also sometimes find their work a bit tougher to get through when my eyes or brain are tired.<br/><br/>Solution: Richard Armitage <i>reading</i> Heyer to me!<br/><br/>Oh man, I have tried several audiobooks but have never gotten into them. Apparently I have i</span>
  <span id="freeText7977266432489578084" style="display:none">This was my first audiobook AND my first Georgette Heyer! I know...it's a bit disgraceful that I've waited this long to read a book from the woman whom many consider to be the creator of the Regency romance, but while I love Jane Austen and other not-modern authors, I also sometimes find their work a bit tougher to get through when my eyes or brain are tired.<br /><br />Solution: Richard Armitage <i>reading</i> Heyer to me!<br /><br />Oh man, I have tried several audiobooks but have never gotten into them. Apparently I have issues with lots of voices. For women, I often don't like how the hero sounds. For men, I don't like if he sounds like my grandfather reading to me...sensual scenes are just AWKWARD. Anyway....well, I did finally find a voice I do like...Richard Armitage's voice is smooth, rich, and young. He is adept at having all his characters have unique voices so I know who is speaking and the women sound right and not like nags or macho. And the hero....Armitage nailed the hero's drawl to perfection.<br /><br />I listened to this story as a buddy read with Andrea and Lacey. We all loved this. Thanks you two!<br /><br />The story was fun, the heroine was strong, and the narrator made the story come alive. While Armitage's voice definitely added to the experience, I will say, it helped that he had a lot of material to work with. Heyer did a great job setting her scenes, building a relationship between Venetia and Damerel, and populating the story with the right number of secondary characters. I felt like I could vividly see and understand what was going on. The only thing I didn't like was a scene at the beginning when Damerel grabs Venetia and doesn't let her go...I didn't really find that romantic. However, from that point on, their relationship develops well and there is definitely a meeting of the minds that I enjoyed (I hate when stories are just about lust). The title of this work is definitely appropriate for the content of the story because it clearly is about Venetia...and she is lovely. She is smart, patient, unafraid to pursue what she wants, and even-tempered. She is an excellent, well-rounded heroine and one I enjoyed enormously. <br /><br />It is important to note that I tried the abridged version since I was a newbie to audio and 5 hours seemed a lot more manageable than your traditional 9-12 hour listen. I'd recommend it for listeners new like me. It was not quite as daunting.<br /><br />Now, despite how lovely this experience was, I've found I do NOT have a preference for audio. In fact, I doubt I'll seek out audiobooks unless I'm listening with others or my eyes are messed up or something. I definitely prefer the written word. However, for works that are older or less accessible, I found that audio is a great way to experience the story as it was intended. I think I'll probably listen to audio for Jane Austen works, poetry, more Heyer, Shakespeare, and other classic works that I stumble across. In these, I think the audio would be preferred.<br /><br />Yay for new experiences! It was a pleasure to discover such a lovely introduction to Heyer and the audiobook world. Now, off to check out what else Armitage has narrated :) Oh, and more Heyer!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7977266432489578084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F1+J/jEXuQDJKWLvtIStSDaKQ47XNmaABcO0GkeFlNIGfH/fDwd7vxd3I4jfhtkQCWZ6zl6oJWT/LaX+EfLebw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GAld4miN7RIbk/ySLKfJRLN7cy6n1gJbsHY0kdFYKzAJKqvDVp0vrcXNvfVHpb0cjJdKbi5IQb9KmCV1hy9hjQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p3/18067.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">Georgette Heyer
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,714
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16850527803130433016">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth' title=' The Black Moth' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Black Moth</a>.<br/><br/>In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer. Rougier later became a barrister and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance nov</span>
  <span id="freeText16850527803130433016" style="display:none">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth" title=" The Black Moth" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer. Rougier later became a barrister and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She wrote one novel using the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Georgian and Regencies romances were inspired by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen" title=" Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jane Austen</a>. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16850527803130433016" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
